Since the AST and HIR are fairly similar, this is mostly a simple procedure,\\n4: //! much like a fold. Where lowering involves a bit more work things get more\\n5: //! interesting and there are some invariants you should know about. These mostly\\n6: //! concern spans and IDs.\\n7: //!\\n8: //! Spans are assigned to AST nodes during parsing and then are modified during\\n9: //! expansion to indicate the origin of a node and the process it went through\\n10: //! being expanded. Unlike\\n13: //! expansion we do not preserve the process of lowering in the spans, so spans\\n14: //! should not be modified here. When creating a new node (as opposed to\\n15: //! \\\"folding\\\" an existing one), create a new ID using `next_id()`.\\n16: //!\\n17: //! You must ensure that IDs are unique. Lowers the AST to the HIR.\n2: //!\n3: //! Since the AST and HIR are fairly similar, this is mostly a simple procedure,\n4: //! much like a fold. Where lowering involves a bit more work things get more\n5: //! interesting and there are some invariants you should know about. These mostly\n6: //! concern spans and IDs.\n7: //!\n8: //! Spans are assigned to AST nodes during parsing and then are modified during\n9: //! expansion to indicate the origin of a node and the process it went through\n10: //! being expanded. IDs are assigned to AST nodes just before lowering.\n11: //!\n12: //! For the simpler lowering steps, IDs and spans should be preserved. Unlike\n13: //! expansion we do not preserve the process of lowering in the spans, so spans\n14: //! should not be modified here. When creating a new node (as opposed to\n15: //! \"folding\" an existing one), create a new ID using `next_id()`.\n16: //!\n17: //! You must ensure that IDs are unique. That means that you should only use the\n18: //! ID from an AST node in a single HIR node (you can assume that AST node-IDs\n19: //! are unique). Every new node must have a unique ID. Avoid cloning HIR nodes.\n20: //! If you do, you must then set the new node's ID to a fresh one.\n21: //!\n22: //! Spans are used for error messages and for tools to map semantics back to\n23: //! source code. It is therefore not as important with spans as IDs to be strict\n24: //! about use (you can't break the compiler by screwing up a span). Obviously, a\n25: //! HIR node can only have a single span. But multiple nodes can have the same\n26: //! span and spans don't need to be kept in order, etc. Where code is preserved\n27: //! by lowering, it should have the same span as in the AST. Where HIR nodes are\n28: //! new it is probably best to give a span for the whole AST node being lowered.\n29: //! All nodes should have real spans; don't use dummy spans. Tools are likely to\n30: //! get confused if the spans from leaf AST nodes occur in multiple places\n31: //! in the HIR, especially for multiple identifiers.\n32: \n33: // tidy-alphabetical-start\n34: #![feature(box_patterns)]\n35: #![feature(if_let_guard)]\n36: // tidy-alphabetical-end\n37: \n38: use std::sync::Arc;\n39: \n40: use rustc_ast::node_id::NodeMap;\n41: use rustc_ast::{self as ast, *};\n42: use rustc_attr_parsing::{AttributeParser, Late, OmitDoc};\n43: use rustc_data_structures::fingerprint::Fingerprint;\n44: use rustc_data_structures::sorted_map::SortedMap;\n45: use rustc_data_structures::stable_hasher::{HashStable, StableHasher};\n46: use rustc_data_structures::sync::spawn;\n47: use rustc_data_structures::tagged_ptr::TaggedRef;\n48: use rustc_errors::{DiagArgFromDisplay, DiagCtxtHandle};\n49: use rustc_hir::def::{DefKind, LifetimeRes, Namespace, PartialRes, PerNS, Res};\n50: use rustc_hir::def_id::{CRATE_DEF_ID, LOCAL_CRATE, LocalDefId};\n51: use rustc_hir::definitions::{DefPathData, DisambiguatorState};\n52: use rustc_hir::lints::DelayedLint;\n53: use rustc_hir::{\n54:     self as hir, AngleBrackets, ConstArg, GenericArg, HirId, ItemLocalMap, LifetimeSource,\n55:     LifetimeSyntax, ParamName, Target, TraitCandidate,\n56: };\n57: use rustc_index::{Idx, IndexSlice, IndexVec};\n58: use rustc_macros::extension;\n59: use rustc_middle::span_bug;\n60: use rustc_middle::ty::{ResolverAstLowering, TyCtxt};\n61: use rustc_session::parse::add_feature_diagnostics;\n62: use rustc_span::symbol::{Ident, Symbol, kw, sym};\n63: use rustc_span::{DUMMY_SP, DesugaringKind, Span};\n64: use smallvec::SmallVec;\n65: use thin_vec::ThinVec;\n66: use tracing::{debug, instrument, trace};\n67: \n68: use crate::errors::{AssocTyParentheses, AssocTyParenthesesSub, MisplacedImplTrait};\n69: \n70: macro_rules! arena_vec {\n71:     ($this:expr; $($x:expr),*) => (\n72:         $this.arena.alloc_from_iter([$($x),*])\n73:     );\n74: }\n75: \n76: mod asm;\n77: mod block;\n78: mod contract;\n79: mod delegation;\n80: mod errors;\n81: mod expr;\n82: mod format;\n83: mod index;\n84: mod item;\n85: mod pat;\n86: mod path;\n87: pub mod stability;\n88: \n89: rustc_fluent_macro::fluent_messages! { \"../messages.ftl\" }\n90: \n91: struct LoweringContext<'a, 'hir> {\n92:     tcx: TyCtxt<'hir>,\n93:     resolver: &'a mut ResolverAstLowering,\n94:     disambiguator: DisambiguatorState,\n95: \n96:     /// Used to allocate HIR nodes.\n97:     arena: &'hir hir::Arena<'hir>,\n98: \n99:     /// Bodies inside the owner being lowered.\n100:     bodies: Vec<(hir::ItemLocalId, &'hir hir::Body<'hir>)>,\n101:     /// `#[define_opaque]` attributes\n102:     define_opaque: Option<&'hir [(Span, LocalDefId)]>,\n103:     /// Attributes inside the owner being lowered.\n104:     attrs: SortedMap<hir::ItemLocalId, &'hir [hir::Attribute]>,\n105:     /// Collect items that were created by lowering the current owner.\n106:     children: Vec<(LocalDefId, hir::MaybeOwner<'hir>)>,\n107: \n108:     contract_ensures: Option<(Span, Ident, HirId)>,\n109: \n110:     coroutine_kind: Option<hir::CoroutineKind>,\n111: \n112:     /// When inside an `async` context, this is the `HirId` of the\n113:     /// `task_context` local bound to the resume argument of the coroutine.\n114:     task_context: Option<HirId>,\n115: \n116:     /// Used to get the current `fn`'s def span to point to when using `await`\n117:     /// outside of an `async fn`.\n118:     current_item: Option<Span>,\n119: \n120:     catch_scope: Option<HirId>,\n121:     loop_scope: Option<HirId>,\n122:     is_in_loop_condition: bool,\n123:     is_in_dyn_type: bool,\n124: \n125:     current_hir_id_owner: hir::OwnerId,\n126:     item_local_id_counter: hir::ItemLocalId,\n127:     trait_map: ItemLocalMap<Box<[TraitCandidate]>>,\n128: \n129:     impl_trait_defs: Vec<hir::GenericParam<'hir>>,\n130:     impl_trait_bounds: Vec<hir::WherePredicate<'hir>>,\n131: \n132:     /// NodeIds of pattern identifiers and labelled nodes that are lowered inside the current HIR owner.\n133:     ident_and_label_to_local_id: NodeMap<hir::ItemLocalId>,\n134:     /// NodeIds that are lowered inside the current HIR owner. src,\n183:             src_span,\n184:             DelimSpacing::new(Spacing::Alone, Spacing::Alone)\n185:         )],\n186:         result: Vec::new(),\n187:         result_stack: Vec::new(),\n188:     };\n189: \n190:     loop {\n191:         // Look at the last frame on the stack.\n192:         // If it still has a TokenTree we have not looked at yet, use that tree.\n193:         let Some(tree) = tscx.stack.last_mut().unwrap().next() else {\n194:             // This else-case never produces a value for `tree` (it `continue`s or `return`s).\n195: \n196:             // Otherwise, if we have just reached the end of a sequence and we can keep repeating,\n197:             // go back to the beginning of the sequence.\n198:             let frame = tscx.stack.last_mut().unwrap();\n199:    if repeat_idx < repeat_len {\n203:                     frame.idx = 0;\n204:                     if let Some(sep) = sep {\n205:                         tscx.result.push(TokenTree::Token(*sep, Spacing::Alone));\n206:                     }\n207:                     continue;\n208:                 }\n209:             }\n210: \n211:             // We are done with the top of the stack. Pop it. Depending on what it was, we do\n212:             // different things. Note that the outermost item must be the delimited, wrapped RHS\n213:             // that was passed in originally to `transcribe`.\n214:             match tscx.stack.pop().unwrap().kind {\n215:                 // Done with a sequence. Pop from repeats.\n216:                 FrameKind::Sequence { .. } => {\n217:                     tscx.repeats.pop();\n218:                 }\n219: \n220:                 // We are done processing a Delimited. If this is the top-level delimited, we are\n221:                 // done. Otherwise, we unwind the result_stack to append what we have produced to\n222:                 // any previous results.\n223:                 FrameKind::Delimited { delim, span, mut spacing, .. } => {\n224:                     // Hack to force-insert a space after `]` in certain case.\n225:                     // See discussion of the `hex-literal` crate in #114571.\n226:                     if delim == Delimiter::Bracket {\n227:                         spacing.close = Spacing::Alone;\n228:                     }\n229:                     if tscx.result_stack.is_empty() {\n230:                         // No results left to compute! This is an NFA-based parser, which calls out to the main Rust parser for named non-terminals\\n2: //! (which it commits to fully when it hits one in a grammar). There's a set of current NFA threads\\n3: //! and a set of next ones. Instead of NTs, we have a special case for Kleene star. The big-O, in\\n4: //! pathological cases, is worse than traditional use of NFA or Earley parsing, but it's an easier\\n5: //! fit for Macro-by-Example-style rules.\\n6: //!\\n7: //! (In order to prevent the pathological case, we'd need to lazily construct the resulting\\n8: //! `NamedMatch`es at the very end. It'd be a pain, and require more memory to keep around old\\n9: //! matcher positions, but it would also save overhead)\\n10: //!\\n11: //! We don't say this parser uses the Earley algorithm, because it's unnecessarily inaccurate.\\n12: //! The macro parser restricts itself to the features of finite state automata. Earley parsers\\n13: //! can be described as an extension of NFAs with completion rules, prediction rules, and recursion.\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Quick intro to how the parser works:\\n16: //!\\n17: //! A \\\"matcher position\\\" (a.k.a. \\\"position\\\" or \\\"mp\\\") is a dot in the middle of a matcher, usually\\n18: //! written as a `·`. For example `· a $( a )* a b` is one, as is `a $( · a )* a b`.\\n19: //!\\n20: //! The parser walks through the input a token at a time, maintaining a list\\n21: //! of threads consistent with the current position in the input string: `cur_mps`.\\n22: //!\\n23: //! As it processes them, it fills up `eof_mps` with threads that would be valid if\\n24: //! the macro invocation is now over, `bb_mps` with threads that are waiting on\\n25: //! a Rust non-terminal like `$e:expr`, and `next_mps` with threads that are waiting\\n26: //! on a particular token. Most of the logic concerns moving the · through the\\n27: //! repetitions indicated by Kleene stars. The rules for moving the · without\\n28: //! consuming any input are called epsilon transitions. It only advances or calls\\n29: //! out to the real Rust parser when no `cur_mps` threads remain.\\n30: //!\\n31: //! Example:\\n32: //!\\n33: //! ```text, ignore\\n34: //! Start parsing a a a a b against [· a $( a )* a b].\\n35: //!\\n36: //! Remaining input: a a a a b\\n37: //! next: [· a $( a )* a b]\\n38: //!\\n39: //! - - - Advance over an a. - - -\\n40: //!\\n41: //! Remaining input: a a a b\\n42: //! cur: [a · $( a )* a b]\\n43: //! \"## Rust Macro Expansion to HIR Lowering Chain\\n\\nThe Rust compiler's macro expansion and HIR lowering process follows a multi-stage pipeline:\\n\\n### Stage 1: Compilation Pipeline Orchestration\\nThe compilation starts in `rustc_interface/src/passes.rs` which sets up the macro expansion configuration and initiates the process by calling `ExtCtxt::monotonic_expander().expand_crate(krate)`.\\n\\n### Stage 2: Macro Expansion Engine\\nThe main expansion logic resides in `rustc_expand/src/expand.rs`. The `MacroExpander` struct orchestrates the entire process:\\n\\n1. **`expand_crate()`** - Entry point that recursively expands all macro invocations in the crate\\n2. **`fully_expand_fragment()`** - Recursively processes AST fragments by collecting macro invocations and replacing them with placeholders, then expanding them\\n3. **`expand_invoc()`** - Dispatcher for individual macro invocations, routing to either procedural or declarative macro handlers based on the `SyntaxExtensionKind`\\n\\n### Stage 3: Procedural Macro Expansion\\nProcedural macros are handled in `rustc_expand/src/proc_macro.rs`:\\n- `BangProcMacro::expand()` - Takes a token stream input and executes the procedural macro code through the proc-macro bridge\\n- `AttrProcMacro::expand_with_safety()` - Handles attribute-like procedural macros\\n\\nThe proc-macro server in `rustc_expand/src/proc_macro_server.rs` provides the runtime bridge for executing external proc-macro code.\\n\\n### Stage 4: Declarative Macro Expansion\\nDeclarative macros (\\\"macro by example\\\") are implemented in `rustc_expand/src/mbe/`:\\n\\n1. **Pattern Matching** (`macro_parser.rs`):\\n   - `TtParser` implements an NFA-based parser that matches macro input against the LHS patterns\\n   - Uses epsilon transitions and Kleene star handling to match token sequences\\n\\n2. **Macro Expansion** (`macro_rules.rs`):\\n   - `MacroRulesMacroExpander::expand()` - Entry point for declarative macros\\n   - `expand_macro()` - Core expansion function that:\\n     - Calls `try_match_macro()` to match input against defined rules\\n     - If matched, calls `transcribe()` to transform the matched tokens\\n\\n3. **Token Stream Transformation** (`transcribe.rs`):\\n   - `transcribe()` - Transforms the matched token patterns by:\\n     - Substituting matched variables into the RHS\\n     - Expanding Kleene repetitions (`*`, `+`, `?`)\\n     - Applying proper spacing and delimiter handling\\n   - `TranscrCtx` - Context manager that maintains the transcription state and result stack\\n\\n### Stage 5: Token Stream to AST Conversion\\nAfter macro expansion, the resulting token stream is converted to AST:\\n\\n1. **`MacroExpander::parse_ast_fragment()`** - Creates a parser from the token stream\\n2. **`parse_ast_fragment()` function** - Parses tokens into appropriate AST fragment types (Items, Stmts, Exprs, etc.)\\n3. **Placeholder Expansion** - Expanded AST is incorporated back into the original AST by replacing placeholder nodes\\n\\n### Stage 6: AST to HIR Lowering\\nOnce all macros are expanded, the AST is lowered to HIR in `rustc_ast_lowering/`:\\n\\n1. **`lower_to_hir()`** (`lib.rs`) - Entry point that:\\n   - Creates an `ItemLowerer` for traversing the expanded AST\\n   - Iterates through all definition IDs and lowers each one\\n\\n2. **Item-Level Lowering** (`item.rs`):\\n   - `ItemLowerer` - Walks through AST items and lowers them to HIR\\n   - `lower_item()` - Lowers individual items\\n   - `lower_node()` - Lowers a specific AST node to HIR\\n\\n3. **Expression and Pattern Lowering**:\\n   - `expr.rs` - Lowers various expression types\\n   - `pat.rs` - Lowers pattern types\\n   - `block.rs` - Lowers block-level constructs\\n\\n### Key Data Structures:\\n- **Token Stream**: Sequence of tokens produced by macros\\n- **AST Fragment**: Expanded AST nodes (Items, Stmts, Exprs, etc.)\\n- **HIR**: Final intermediate representation used for type checking and later compilation stages\\n- **NamedMatch**: Captured subexpressions during macro pattern matching\\n\\nThe entire process maintains proper hygiene information (via `SyntaxContext` and expansion IDs) to ensure correct name resolution and proper error reporting throughout the pipeline.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2075,"cache_read_input_tokens":78243,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2075},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c57019fb-664e-441c-9918-458584d000c3","uuid":"87defe89-02dd-403e-8382-c007382dedd6"}

Orchestration\\nThe compilation starts in `rustc_interface/src/passes.rs` which sets up the macro expansion configuration and initiates the process by calling `ExtCtxt::monotonic_expander().expand_crate(krate)`.\\n\\n### Stage 2: Macro Expansion Engine\\nThe main expansion logic resides in `rustc_expand/src/expand.rs`. The `MacroExpander` struct orchestrates the entire process:\\n\\n1. **`expand_crate()`** - Entry point that recursively expands all macro invocations in the crate\\n2. **`fully_expand_fragment()`** - Recursively processes AST fragments by collecting macro invocations and replacing them with placeholders, then expanding them\\n3. **`expand_invoc()`** - Dispatcher for individual macro invocations, routing to either procedural or declarative macro handlers based on the `SyntaxExtensionKind`\\n\\n### Stage 3: Procedural Macro Expansion\\nProcedural macros are handled in `rustc_expand/src/proc_macro.rs`:\\n- `BangProcMacro::expand()` - Takes a token stream input and executes the procedural macro code through the proc-macro bridge\\n- `AttrProcMacro::expand_with_safety()` - Handles attribute-like procedural macros\\n\\nThe proc-macro server in `rustc_expand/src/proc_macro_server.rs` provides the runtime bridge for executing external proc-macro code.\\n\\n### Stage 4: Declarative Macro Expansion\\nDeclarative macros (\\\"macro by example\\\") are implemented in `rustc_expand/src/mbe/`:\\n\\n1. **Pattern Matching** (`macro_parser.rs`):\\n   - If matched, calls `transcribe()` to transform the matched tokens\\n\\n3. **Token Stream Transformation** (`transcribe.rs`):\\n   - `transcribe()` - Transforms the matched token patterns by:\\n     - Substituting matched variables into the RHS\\n     - Expanding Kleene repetitions (`*`, `+`, `?`)\\n     - Applying proper spacing and delimiter handling\\n   - `TranscrCtx` - Context manager that maintains the transcription state and result stack\\n\\n### Stage 5: Token Stream to AST Conversion\\nAfter macro expansion, the resulting token stream is converted to AST:\\n\\n1. **`MacroExpander::parse_ast_fragment()`** - Creates a parser from the token stream\\n2. **`parse_ast_fragment()` function** - Parses tokens into appropriate AST fragment types (Items, Stmts, Exprs, etc.)\\n3. **Placeholder Expansion** - Expanded AST is incorporated back into the original AST by replacing placeholder nodes\\n\\n### Stage 6: AST to HIR Lowering\\nOnce all macros are expanded, the AST is lowered to HIR in `rustc_ast_lowering/`:\\n\\n1. **`lower_to_hir()`** (`lib.rs`) -
